.cs1-kern-left{padding-left:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .cs1-kern-right{padding-right:0.2em}.mw-parser-output .citation .mw-selflink{font-weight:inherit}</style><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-7-5600-0739-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-7-5600-0739-7">978-7-5600-0739-7</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-153">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jiàndào is the pronunciation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Chinese" title="Modern Standard Chinese">Modern Standard Chinese</a>, deriving from the <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Mandarin_(division_of_Mandarin)" title="Beijing Mandarin (division of Mandarin)">Beijing Mandarin</a>. There are other pronunciations of the <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Chinese" title="Varieties of Chinese">varieties of Chinese</a>, deriving its pronunciation from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Chinese" title="Middle Chinese">Middle Chinese</a>, as like:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Min" title="Southern Min">Southern Min</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwan</a>): kiàm-tō (<a href="/wiki/Pe%CC%8Dh-%C5%8De-j%C4%AB" title="Pe̍h-ōe-jī">Pe̍h-ōe-jī</a> / kiàm-tō (<a href="/wiki/T%C3%A2i-u%C3%A2n_L%C3%B4-m%C3%A1-j%C4%AB_Phing-im_Hong-%C3%A0n" title="Tâi-uân Lô-má-jī Phing-im Hong-àn">Tâi-uân Lô-má-jī Phing-im Hong-àn</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hakka_Chinese" title="Hakka Chinese">Hakka Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sixian_dialect" title="Sixian dialect">Sixian dialect</a>): kiam-tho (<a href="/wiki/Pha%CC%8Dk-fa-s%E1%B9%B3" title="Pha̍k-fa-sṳ">Pha̍k-fa-sṳ</a>) / giam-to (<a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hakka_Romanization_System" title="Taiwanese Hakka Romanization System">Taiwanese Hakka Romanization System</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Yue_Chinese" title="Yue Chinese">Yue Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Cantonese" title="Hong Kong Cantonese">Hong Kong</a>): gim<sup>3</sup>-dou<sup>6</sup> (<a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[141]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wu_Chinese" title="Wu Chinese">Wu Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Shanghainese" title="Shanghainese">Shanghainese</a>): cie<sup>3</sup>-dau<sup>2</sup> (<a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Wu_Chinese" title="Romanization of Wu Chinese">Romanization of Wu Chinese</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wu_Chinese" title="Wu Chinese">Wu Chinese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Suzhou_dialect" title="Suzhou dialect">Suzhou dialect</a>): cie<sup>523</sup>-dau<sup>231</sup> (<a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Wu_Chinese" title="Romanization of Wu Chinese">Romanization of Wu Chinese</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[145]</a></sup></li></ul>
</span></li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1 cs1-prop-script cs1-prop-foreign-lang-source"><a class="external text" href="http://zhongwen.com/d/164/x93.htm" rel="nofollow">"Yě" <bdi lang="zh">也</bdi></a>. <i>zhongwen.com</i> (in Chinese)<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">17 February</span> 2015</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=zhongwen.com&amp;rft.atitle=Y%C4%9B+%E4%B9%9F&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fzhongwen.com%2Fd%2F164%2Fx93.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChinese+characters"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-36"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-36">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i><a href="/wiki/Shuowen_Jiezi" title="Shuowen Jiezi">Shuowen Jiezi</a></i> gives the origin of 也 as "女陰也", or 'female <i>yin</i> [organ]'.  (The 也 in the definition itself is a declarative sentence final particle.)  By the Classical period (6th century BC), the original definition had fallen into disuse, and all appearances of the character in texts of that period and in later in Literary Chinese use it as a phonetic loan for the grammatical particle.  In addition to serving as a classical particle, it has acquired the modern Vernacular Chinese meaning of 'also'.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-80">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"...East Asia had been among the first regions of the world to produce written records of the past. Well into modern times Chinese script, the common script across East Asia, served—with local adaptations and variations—as the normative medium of record-keeping and written historical narrative, as well as official communication. This was true, not only in China itself, but in Korea, Japan, and Vietnam." The Oxford History of Historical Writing. Volume 3. Jose Rabasa, Masayuki Sato, Edoardo Tortarolo, Daniel Woolf – 1400–1800, p. 2.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation news cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://jx.people.com.cn/n2/2021/0409/c186330-34666372.html" rel="nofollow">"《国际中文教育中文水平等级标准》来了 汉语水平考试会有啥变化"</a>. 人民网-人民日报海外版. 9 April 2021. <q>日前，《国际中文教育中文水平等级标准》（GF0025-2021）（下称《标准》）由教育部、国家语言文字工作委员会发布，作为国家语委语言文字规范自2021年7月1日起正式实施。......汉语水平考试（HSK）自1984年开创以来已走过37年，经历了基础、初中等、高等"3等11级"的HSK1.0和"一级到六级"6个级别的HSK2.0两个阶段，即将迎来"三等九级"的HSK3.0新阶段。</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=%E3%80%8A%E5%9B%BD%E9%99%85%E4%B8%AD%E6%96%87%E6%95%99%E8%82%B2%E4%B8%AD%E6%96%87%E6%B0%B4%E5%B9%B3%E7%AD%89%E7%BA%A7%E6%A0%87%E5%87%86%E3%80%8B%E6%9D%A5%E4%BA%86+%E6%B1%89%E8%AF%AD%E6%B0%B4%E5%B9%B3%E8%80%83%E8%AF%95%E4%BC%9A%E6%9C%89%E5%95%A5%E5%8F%98%E5%8C%96&amp;rft.date=2021-04-09&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fjx.people.com.cn%2Fn2%2F2021%2F0409%2Fc186330-34666372.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChinese+characters"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://coct.naer.edu.tw/TBCL/" rel="nofollow">"Taiwan Benchmarks for the Chinese Language"</a>. <i>華語文語料庫與標準體系整合應用系統</i>. 國家教育研究院. <q>The TBCL sets out <b>seven levels of Chinese language proficiency</b> in the five skills: listening, speaking, reading, writing and translating. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_and_construction_of_Chinese_characters">History and construction of Chinese characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: History and construction of Chinese characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>Excerpt from <a class="external text" href="http://www.pinyin.info/readings/texts/visible/index.html" rel="nofollow">Visible Speech: The Diverse Oneness of Writing Systems</a> by John DeFrancis, 1989 by the University of Hawai'i Press. Used by permission of the University of Hawai'i Press.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_dictionaries_and_character_reference">Online dictionaries and character reference</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Online dictionaries and character reference">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://ctext.org/dictionary.pl?if=en" rel="nofollow">Chinese Text Project Dictionary</a> Comprehensive character dictionary including data for all Chinese characters in Unicode, and exemplary usage from early Chinese texts.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.omniglot.com/chinese/evolution.htm" rel="nofollow">Evolution of Chinese Characters</a></li>
<li>Richard Sears, <a class="external text" href="https://hanziyuan.net/" rel="nofollow">Chinese Etymology</a></li>
<li>Da, Jun, <a class="external text" href="https://lingua.mtsu.edu/chinese-computing/" rel="nofollow">Chinese text computing</a> – statistics on use of Chinese characters</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinese_characters_in_computing">Chinese characters in computing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chinese_characters&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Chinese characters in computing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://www.unicode.org/charts/unihan.html" rel="nofollow">Unihan Database</a>: Chinese, Japanese, and Korean references, readings, and meanings for all the Chinese and Chinese-derived characters in the <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> character set</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="http://www.cymraeg.ru/daoulagad.html" rel="nofollow">Daoulagad Han</a> – Mobile OCR hanzi dictionary, OCR interface to the UniHan database</li></ul>
